<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_867f8e84-25b0-4a4a-a6fa-cdc48b24f1c9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="review_2739189442" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2739189442" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2739189442?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2739189442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15775734302659372167">This is the first volume I had to read in German because for some crazy reason my library only has Vol. 1 – 14 in English. If I’m entirely honest it was kind of weird to read <b>“Fruits Basket”</b> in German but oh well, I’ll hopefully get used to it because there are at least 8 volumes left. XD<br/>I guess I better be grateful they even have the entire series, right? *lol*<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Thoughts to the highlights of this volume:</u>
</b><br/><br/>- Can I say how much I dislike Akito! He makes me so angry! Is there even one zodiac membe</span>
  <span id="freeText15775734302659372167" style="display:none">This is the first volume I had to read in German because for some crazy reason my library only has Vol. 1 – 14 in English. If I’m entirely honest it was kind of weird to read <b>“Fruits Basket”</b> in German but oh well, I’ll hopefully get used to it because there are at least 8 volumes left. XD<br />I guess I better be grateful they even have the entire series, right? *lol*<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Thoughts to the highlights of this volume:</u>
</b><br /><br />- Can I say how much I dislike Akito! He makes me so angry! Is there even one zodiac member he hasn’t physically or mentally abused? It seems like they all fear him, but poor Yuki and Kyo certainly had to suffer the most. My heart ached for Yuki so much… T_T Poor boy! <br /><br />- Plus I think after reading this volume it’s safe to say that Yuki isn’t in love with Tohru but that he <b>
  <u>loves</u>
</b> her instead. Yes, there is a difference. Their relationship is more like a big sister and her little brother so I doubt there’ll ever be any romance between them. XD Which would make Kyo the final love interest and I’d be so happy about this! *lol*<br /><br />- <b>I. STILL. LIVE. AND. BREATHE. FOR. THOSE. TINY. LITTLE. TOHRU. AND. KYO. MOMENTS!</b> &lt;333 I swear whenever Kyo gets closer to her I’m like: AHHHHHHHHHH!!!!! *hearty eyes* &lt;333<br /><br />- Their version of Cinderella was hilarious!!! *LOL* I had to laugh so hard. Hana-chan was such a funny Cinderella. Always thinking about food instead of her prince. XD <br /><br />- I think there might be a growing romance between Yuki and Machi? I mean in contrast to all the other girls and boys at their school she’s completely unimpressed by Yuki, yet she seems to know him better than anyone else. Machi sees right through his façade and she knows that he’s lonely. So I’d definitely be on board of this ship! He’d so deserve a person that loves him for who he is and not for who people believe him to be! &lt;333</span>
  <a data-text-id="15775734302659372167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_177931003" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177931003" />
    <a title="Rain Misoa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4481312-rain-misoa"><img alt="Rain Misoa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305629680p2/4481312.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177931003?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rain Misoa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rain Misoa" href="/user/show/4481312-rain-misoa">Rain Misoa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE!!! And people who wants to get to know Yuki better~</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rain by: </span>
      Nicole Terazue
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4481312-rain-misoa?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177931003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3656833301886378115">Tee-Hee-Hee! This volume was adorable. Well, towards the end it was. The beginning made me want to cry. However, it's because of this sadness, I think, that made me understand a little bit better. That's right... I actually understand Yuki a little better now. Took me long enough, ne? Well, I'm sorry but arrogance makes me dislike people. In any case, I really appreciate what this volume does for the reader. It makes things so much more clearer and also brings the reader to a place where you thi</span>
  <span id="freeText3656833301886378115" style="display:none">Tee-Hee-Hee! This volume was adorable. Well, towards the end it was. The beginning made me want to cry. However, it's because of this sadness, I think, that made me understand a little bit better. That's right... I actually understand Yuki a little better now. Took me long enough, ne? Well, I'm sorry but arrogance makes me dislike people. In any case, I really appreciate what this volume does for the reader. It makes things so much more clearer and also brings the reader to a place where you think things are going haywire but is also going towards peace at the same time. That's not to say things aren't going to go crazy again. It just wouldn't be <i>Fruits Basket</i> without all them insane plot twists! <br /><br />What can I say? I think Takaya-sensei did a fabulous job in creating this story. What she made Yuki go through and how she made him feel... that was the most brilliant thing I have ever seen happen in any manga I've read (and I've read quite a few). Reading this particular volume made me understand Yuki a lot more. I'm glad she did that for people, like me, who might have thought that Yuki was just being selfish. I've said this before and I'll say it again, I never hated Yuki. I did like him. I was just confused as to why he was acting the way he acted. Sensei did amazing in helping me, and perhaps many others, see who he truly was. *Happy sigh* So glad! Another thing is I approve of her version of <i>Cinderella</i> a whole lot more than the real one. XD It just suits me a lot more. X3 What can I say? I'm a women who believes you can do whatever you want! But that's all I'll say about that. This is definitely something you should read for yourself. Especially if you don't normally agree with the norm! ^_^<br /><br />Yuki, Yuki, Yuki. This volume mostly centered around Yuki. And I'm glad for it! We get to see more about his past. Him being alone for most of his childhood... how he was revered highly yet not known for his suffering... it was very heart-breaking indeed. I had no clue this poor boy went through all that. I mean, I knew it couldn't have been fun being locked up in a dark room but... my ignorance didn't help me understand completely. Now I do and I love Yuki all the more for it! (Yes. It is official. Stop bothering me.) You want to know what I find more amazing? The fact that Yuki is growing so much as a person. He said he wanted to change and, my God, is he changing! He's trying his best to reach out to Kyo and make peace with him. It's so... lovely. He surprised me a lot of the time whenever he tried to do something he normally wouldn't do. As for Kyo... he needs more time. Yes, he's improving as well but because of all the negativity he received as a child, his relationship is still rocky when it comes to Yuki. But I do get the feeling he is warming up to him. It's not as heavy... not as strained... I think for now he's trying to focus on what's going on between him and Tohru... which brings me to my next question: WHAT THE HELL IS GOING ON THERE!? I'm so confused! He knows something and he's just not saying it! He better say it soon because it's driving me insane!!! &gt;_&lt; And Akito is a prick. *Still has no pity for the asswipe*<br /><br />Tohru is another character still growing. In a lot of ways, she's still herself from when the series first started out. However, she's able now to talk to people when things are bothering her without seeming like a nuisance. She still worries about her friends and... *Smirks* ...we are beginning to see what it's like to be in love~ Yay!!! She's so keen to other's feelings. She sees that Uo still misses Kureno, that Yuki is growing, and that Kyo is acting strangely. I demand to know what's wrong with him! Anyway, I love her and I have a feeling things are going to get a bit more complicated for her... oh joy... Machi is another weird character. She's not impressed with Yuki which makes me happy, yes, because it's different but I would still like to know her reasons for it. I'm just curious. Such an enigma, that one. Manabe... I love how he teases Yuki. He makes me giggle. Haru, Momiji, Kisa, and Hiro are just cute as hell. Their relationship with each other is very strong. As it should be! Haru... you were a genius to tell Shishou about the play! Very worth it! &gt;:3 As for Hanajima, I couldn't imagine a much better Cinderella. Oh, my... her and Shishou! That's just so cute! Too bad Kyo doesn't approve... OH WELL! WE SHALL MAKE HIM!!! MWAHAHAHAHAHAHAHAHA!!! &gt;:3<br /><br />I am losing it... let me wrap this up before any more of my brain cells die. This book is filled with a lot of Yuki's history that helps the reader a lot when it comes to getting the full picture. It's hilarious and getting a lot more romantic as well! I cannot wait to see more of the smexy! EEEE!!! I'm excited! So yeah! If you like romance, hilarity to the extreme, and AWESOME characters and plot twists, then you really should invest into this type of manga. It really is amazing and I'm sure you will not regret getting into this series. I know I am dying to find out why Kyo is acting so weird and whether the other characters will get their happy ending. I must know, damn it! *Ahem* Well, I've babbled for long enough. I'm going to get ready and journey into the 16th volume of Furuba! Hurry up and meet me there! *Winks*</span>
  <a data-text-id="3656833301886378115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer279036456&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279036456" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12496892707105094949"><b>Favourite Character:</b> Shigure<br/><br/>While recovering from his panic attack, Yuki tells Kakeru about his relationship with Tohru. In a flashback, Yuki remembers his childhood under Akito's control, believing he was despised by the rest of the zodiac. When Yuki sought out Kyo, as the similarly despised cat, Kyo scorned him as the rat that tricked the original cat. In the depth of his despair, he ran away; while outside, he helped a lost girl, Tohru, return home (giving her the treasured cap as he did so),</span>
  <span id="freeText12496892707105094949" style="display:none"><b>Favourite Character:</b> Shigure<br /><br />While recovering from his panic attack, Yuki tells Kakeru about his relationship with Tohru. In a flashback, Yuki remembers his childhood under Akito's control, believing he was despised by the rest of the zodiac. When Yuki sought out Kyo, as the similarly despised cat, Kyo scorned him as the rat that tricked the original cat. In the depth of his despair, he ran away; while outside, he helped a lost girl, Tohru, return home (giving her the treasured cap as he did so), which gave him proof that he was not as useless as Akito claimed. In the present, Yuki admits to Kakeru that what he wants from Tohru is the unconditional, nurturing love of "a mother," not the love of a woman, and yet despite this he is jealous of the growing attraction of Tohru and Kyo. Meanwhile, during rehearsals for Cinderella, their class realizes that their leads are miscast, with Kyo incapable of being charming as a prince, nor Tohru wicked as a stepsister, nor Hanajima a downtrodden Cinderella. The play is rewritten as Sorta Cinderella and the performance is successful, despite personal, out-of-character outbursts by Tohru, Kyo, and Uotani. At Tohru's request, Momiji makes a copy of the play's video for Kureno, so that he can see Uotani's outcry that he come see her. Meanwhile, Yuki sees some girls bullying Machi for saying that Yuki is not a prince, which she counters by saying she believes that Yuki is lonely in spite of being surrounded by others. Before anything else can happen, Kakeru comes to save her. Meanwhile, Kyo begins to wonder if Tohru is starting to like him, but he brushes off that thought.</span>

        <a title="Kailey (BooksforMKs)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kailey (BooksforMKs)" href="/user/show/5836046-kailey-booksformks">Kailey (BooksforMKs)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5836046-kailey-booksformks?shelf=graphic-novels-and-manga">graphic-novels-and-manga</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638927535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13451397058808420733">In this volume we get a lot more backstory on Yuki's childhood, and the emotional and verbal abuse that he underwent from his parents and from Akito. Poor Yuki! Through all the memories that Yuki is fighting through, he realizes the nature of his true feelings for Tohru, and it was not quite what I expected!<br/><br/>We also see a flashback to when Kyo and Yuki first met as children, so that was especially heart-wrenching since they've almost been tolerating each other lately. Kyo is mostly sulking and br</span>
  <span id="freeText13451397058808420733" style="display:none">In this volume we get a lot more backstory on Yuki's childhood, and the emotional and verbal abuse that he underwent from his parents and from Akito. Poor Yuki! Through all the memories that Yuki is fighting through, he realizes the nature of his true feelings for Tohru, and it was not quite what I expected!<br /><br />We also see a flashback to when Kyo and Yuki first met as children, so that was especially heart-wrenching since they've almost been tolerating each other lately. Kyo is mostly sulking and brooding, and the only thing that will bring him out of his shell is Tohru.<br /><br />I was interested to find out more about the strange power that Akito has over all the Sohma family, why he is head of the family, and why no matter how much he abuses them, the zodiac members never blame Akito or fight back. It's all mystical curses, and creepy history going back hundreds of years.<br /><br />Tohru and her classmates are putting on a play, Cinderella, for the school festival, but no one gets parts that match their personalities, so they rewrite the play into something that is easier for them to act. It's hilarious and wonderful and I was laughing my head off!<br /><br />This series addresses some issues like abandonment and feelings of loneliness, of not belonging or not being needed, and it really touched a lot of deep emotions in me and made me connect with the characters. I’m so emotional about it, but I love the journey the characters go on to find healing and happiness!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13451397058808420733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText266029430122672743" style="display:none">This volume actually provided me with several laugh out loud moments. Yay! The epic play, "Sorta Cinderella," was certainly one for the ages. Heh, at this point in my life I found the closing lines of the play particularly delightful, "And so Cinderella chose a path with no princes. And her yakiniku shop was blessed with good business. After proving that a woman can live a full life without marriage, she most certainly lived happily ever after." Hee!<br /><br />This volume also makes me really sad that the word angstrom is a measure of distance. I'd like to repurpose it as a measurement of angst. LOL, as in, Yuki's backstory in this volume had an angstrom of 11 (on a scale of 10). Poor lil' abused guy. <br /><br />Finally, I read a first printing hot off the presses from Tokyopop back in 2006. And what a terrible print job it was. The whole transfer was done with a very violent hand. Ugh. Very sloppy and quite distracting. I'm hoping the rest of the volumes aren't so ugly.</span>

<div id="review_145503187" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/430329-alison-alisoncanread?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145503187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer370035989519691907">Yet another Yuki-heavy volume. As much as I love Yun-Yun, I'm really missing Kyo. We learn more about Yuki's childhood in this volume. He was placed with Akito at an early age. Akito must not be much older than Yuki, because they were both children together. Even as a child, Akito was selfish, needy, and cruel. He made sure that Yuki understood "his place." He was worthless. No one wanted him. The one time Yuki tried to make friends in school, he accidentally turned into a rat, and all his new f</span>
  <span id="freeText370035989519691907" style="display:none">Yet another Yuki-heavy volume. As much as I love Yun-Yun, I'm really missing Kyo. We learn more about Yuki's childhood in this volume. He was placed with Akito at an early age. Akito must not be much older than Yuki, because they were both children together. Even as a child, Akito was selfish, needy, and cruel. He made sure that Yuki understood "his place." He was worthless. No one wanted him. The one time Yuki tried to make friends in school, he accidentally turned into a rat, and all his new friends' memories had to be modified. This only served to reinforce Yuki's isolation and feelings of worthlessness. Tohru managed to unknowingly boost Yuki's self-esteem before she even knew him. When they were both small, Tohru wandered away from her mother; Yuki helped her find her way. In that moment, he felt needed.<br /><br />Yuki finally realizes his feelings for Tohru. This is super-weird to me. He thinks of her as his mother. The only person who ever cared for him. I find this a little hard to believe. How many 18 year old guys decide that a pretty girl whom they adore is the functional equivalent of their mother?<br /><br />The rest of the volume as another attempt at levity. Tohru, Yuki, Kyo, Uo-chan, and Hana-chan are starring in the class production of Cinderella. This was the best Cinderella production I've ever seen. It's specifically called "Sorta Cinderella." They had to change the story since Tohru is incapable of being an evil stepsister, Kyo isn't exactly prince charming, and goth Hana-chan is far from sweet Cinderella. My favorite part was when Yuki, the fairy godmother asked Cinderella if he could grant her a wish and she requested to "burn the palace down." Cinderella was more interested in eating dinner than dancing with the prince. A lot of Fruits Basket funny moments fall flat for me, but this was fantastic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="370035989519691907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264105225" />
    <a title="Jessica-Robyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3235169-jessica-robyn"><img alt="Jessica-Robyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581748596p2/3235169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/264105225?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica-Robyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica-Robyn" href="/user/show/3235169-jessica-robyn">Jessica-Robyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3235169-jessica-robyn?shelf=manga-manhwa">manga-manhwa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264105225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6027779740597342437">This volume has two very different moods to it. <br/><br/>The first part is very sad as we go more into Yuki's history, how he ended up under Akito's control, and some of what that entailed. This was a great follow up to what ended off the last volume. The more I learn about Yuki the more I'm starting to love him. After everything everyone in this series has experienced all you want is for them to be happy in the future. This new information also brings a lot more weight to Tohru's presence and how by jus</span>
  <span id="freeText6027779740597342437" style="display:none">This volume has two very different moods to it. <br /><br />The first part is very sad as we go more into Yuki's history, how he ended up under Akito's control, and some of what that entailed. This was a great follow up to what ended off the last volume. The more I learn about Yuki the more I'm starting to love him. After everything everyone in this series has experienced all you want is for them to be happy in the future. This new information also brings a lot more weight to Tohru's presence and how by just being around the Sohma's she really has exposed them to an acceptance that few of them have ever experienced. Although that is a running theme, her interactions with Yuki shows that acceptance in the one of the most poignant ways.<br /><br />The second half of this volume has a very major change in tone. From the dark to the light, the group is set to act out a revised Cinderella play "Sorta Cinderella" for the school culture festival. Through this half I could not stop laughing, as always Takaya gets me with her hilarious blunt dialog and then brings it home by throwing in something meaningful to the characters. A cultural festival play is a common thing to see in a romance manga for obvious reasons (normally used as some sort of filler piece), but this time around "Sorta Cinderella" was full of some of the biggest laughs I've had in the entire series so far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6027779740597342437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5206083668835714826">I think this may be one of my favorite volumes of Fruits Basket. We learn more about Yuki's childhood and his connection to Tohru. You really do understand why Yuki acts the way he does. I really liked seeing the class play they put on, and some of the trouble they had with it. Tohru's really changing: she's still herself, and in a lot of ways, she's still the same Tohru we met at the beginning of the series.   <span id="freeText5206083668835714826" style="display:none">I think this may be one of my favorite volumes of Fruits Basket. We learn more about Yuki's childhood and his connection to Tohru. You really do understand why Yuki acts the way he does. I really liked seeing the class play they put on, and some of the trouble they had with it. Tohru's really changing: she's still herself, and in a lot of ways, she's still the same Tohru we met at the beginning of the series. But she's also speaking up for herself a little more, which is great to see.<br /><br />I, of course, loved the artwork. And the fan art is amazing too. I really do like seeing what the fans come up with.<br /><br />I give it a 5 out of 5.</span>

<div id="review_2602037703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2602037703" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54034290-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559532202p2/54034290.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2602037703?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/54034290-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54034290-kelly?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54034290-kelly?shelf=comics-manga">comics-manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2602037703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14837275466369836720">Warm greetings fellow readers and Fruits Basket fans!<br/><br/>	Welcome to volume 15! This one is hands down one of my favorites in the entire series… (and yet it has my least favorite character on the cover… Or at least my favorite character to despise.) Anyway for anyone who hasn’t read my FB reviews, I will say I can’t hold back my enthusiasm for this series so I will be going into spoilers for all volumes and potentially the sequels, so the short version is: It is a fantastically layered series with g</span>
  <span id="freeText14837275466369836720" style="display:none">Warm greetings fellow readers and Fruits Basket fans!<br /><br />	Welcome to volume 15! This one is hands down one of my favorites in the entire series… (and yet it has my least favorite character on the cover… Or at least my favorite character to despise.) Anyway for anyone who hasn’t read my FB reviews, I will say I can’t hold back my enthusiasm for this series so I will be going into spoilers for all volumes and potentially the sequels, so the short version is: It is a fantastically layered series with great character and interesting plot twists: go read it!<br /><br />	And now onto my thoughts and impressions in this volume!<br /><br /><br />	As we said last volume, this one picks up right where 14 left off, with Yuki telling Kakeru about his childhood. Just before we dive into that, I wanted to say that I love that Yuki has a friend he can open up to now; and it is such an unlikely friendship! Maybe he feels comfortable opening up to ‘Nabe-kun because he is so far removed from the whole situation with the Juunishi? I don’t know, but it’s a sweet touch.<br />Yuki starts by saying his earliest memories are all of Akito. That his mother dropped him off to be Akito’s playmate when he was very young. As I said with Isuzu in the last volume, I really think Takaya-Sensei did a great job with Yuki’s backstory; it greatly explains why he was who he was at the start of the series and how he has grown to be who he is. Anyway things quickly go downhill. Yuki is kept isolated both from the outside world and other people. There is one chilling panel when he realizes he has never even met the boy who is his older brother. To make matters worse he is constantly subjected to Akito’s fits of temper; and one day Akito snaps completely. <br />He begins to swipe at the wall with thick black paint telling Yuki “My world is a black place, I have to make my room match.” (Incidentally, I think this is why Yuki had such a visceral reaction when Kakeru pronounces himself as ‘black’ when they are picking ‘Ranger’ colors.) He then begins to rant and rail about how he, Akito, is necessary and needed but Yuki is ‘just his toy.’ He tells Yuki that his mother gave him away and that everyone hates the rat. “If I didn’t care about you, there would be no reason for you to be alive. <br />I have to pause for a second to reflect on just how messed up that is; just - - on every level. First that a child is being told this, by another child. How damaging would that be for the one hearing it? How damaged does the other child have to be to say such a thing? Completely heart wrenching :(<br />Yuki is greatly disturbed by the episode. It doesn’t help when he encounters a young Kyo, who unbeknownst to Yuki has just undergone his own trauma and Kyo too takes all his pain and ire out on Yuki. (Geez!! Can I give this poor baby a hug please??) Yuki desperately tries to reach out for help; first to his mother, who slaps him (cold hearted, social climbing witch… Is it sad that she doesn’t even make the top three for worst parents in this series though?) and sends him back to Akito, and then to Ayame, his brother, who shrugs him off. <br />Things continue to spiral down. Yuki’s physical health and spirit decline. Then one day, he suddenly decides to run away. He runs as far and fast as he is able, for what purpose he doesn’t know— until he spots a mother speaking to two police men. The woman cries how her daughter has been gone all night and what will she do. Remembering, Yuki back-tracks and finds the little girl. He carefully leads her back home. And then it hits him, as he collapses from exhaustion and turns into his rat form, or this case an itty-baby mousey (seriously, it’s so cute!), he thinks ‘Just for a moment, he was necessary.’ That little girl (who yes, was Tohru) was depending on him. He was needed. He had found his own light in the darkness, and that is something Akito could never take away.<br />He then tells Kakeru that as life began to twist him up again, Tohru returned to him. She shone brighter than any darkness life could throw at him. She always listened to his complaints without judgement and continued to be there for him no matter what. After reading Yuki’s past it is completely understandable why Yuki was craving this kind of unconditional love. He had never received it from anyone before. The type of love people usually get from parents, he found in Tohru. (He says he was looking for a ‘mother’ in Tohru, but was confused when he began to see her as a girl he could like too. I think that ultimately though, he loves Tohru as family; a mother, a sister, someone he can depend on.) It’s also understandable that after finally having found that love that he is in no great hurry to give it up. He knows also that Kyo loves Tohru and will either take her away from him, or worse, break her heart and snuff out the light of her happiness forever. (I’m sorry, that probably sounds totally cheesy, but it really is a sweet and well written aspect of the story!)<br /><br /><br />Whew! Oh wow that was dark and depressing! But it really is a great section! My favorite, however it the one that follows:<br /><br />Preparations for the cultural festival continue! But unfortunately for class D-2 they are not going very well. Rehearsals for Cinderella are a disaster. Both Hana and Kyo have no interest in being anything other than themselves, Kinoshita-san is getting a little too into her role as the Wicked Stepmother, and poor Tohru can’t stop crying about how mean her lines are as the Wicked Stepsister. <br />Not all is lost though! Ayame and Mine burst onto the scene with their usual panache, ready to due the costumes (at Yuki’s request, I might add!) Ayame is sorely disappointed that he won’t be able to design a slender and delicate Prince costume for his baby brother (did that sound as creepy as I thin it did?), but accepts the challenge of turning Kyo into a dashing and slender Prince. Meanwhile Mine is in her element and delighted when Hana asks her to make her ballgown ‘pure black’. <br />Since unconventional is on the table, the director proclaims: “Fine! If the story fails with a miscast, then I’ll make the story fit the cast!” And thus: ‘Sorta Cinderella’ is born! And it is great!<br />Cultural Festival day arrives, along with a very confused Kisa and Hiro who have come to watch the show. We get to experience it in the audience with them along with Haru and a very enthusiastic Momiji! (P.s.: Kisa interacting with her ‘big brother’ cousins is just too stinking cute for words!) I won’t spoil the play here, because it is just too much fun! But rest assured it is a very fun episode in this series.<br /><br />A few more little sparkling gems before we part as Yuki’s budding relationship with Machi and how she sees him with unclouded eyes (unlike the rest of the female student body), audience reactions during the play, And Hana-chan getting her flirt on with Shishou! &gt;o&lt; (Incidentally, Kyo had forbidden Tohru from telling Shishou about the show, because he was embarrassed. Luckily, Haru knew Kazuma would like nothing better than to see his foster-son branch out a bit.)<br /><br />Aaaaaand dang that was a lot! See you again in volume 16! Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14837275466369836720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2743599520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2743599520" />
    <a title="Ben Truong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77170844-ben-truong"><img alt="Ben Truong" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2743599520?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ben Truong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ben Truong" href="/user/show/77170844-ben-truong">Ben Truong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77170844-ben-truong?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2743599520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8132245793644907217"><i>Fruits Basket, Vol. 15</i> continues where the previous tankōbon left off and contains the next six chapters (84–89) of the on-going manga series.<br/><br/>While recovering from his panic attack, Yuki Sohma tells Kakeru Manabe about his relationship with Tohru Honda. In a flashback, Yuki remembers his childhood under Akito Sohma's control, believing he was despised by the rest of the zodiac. When Yuki sought out Kyo Sohma, as the similarly despised cat, Kyo scorned him as the Rat that tricked the original cat</span>
  <span id="freeText8132245793644907217" style="display:none"><i>Fruits Basket, Vol. 15</i> continues where the previous tankōbon left off and contains the next six chapters (84–89) of the on-going manga series.<br /><br />While recovering from his panic attack, Yuki Sohma tells Kakeru Manabe about his relationship with Tohru Honda. In a flashback, Yuki remembers his childhood under Akito Sohma's control, believing he was despised by the rest of the zodiac. When Yuki sought out Kyo Sohma, as the similarly despised cat, Kyo scorned him as the Rat that tricked the original cat.<br /><br />In the depth of his despair, he ran away, while outside, he helped a lost girl, Tohru, return home, giving her the treasured cap as he did so, which gave him proof that he was not as useless as Akito claimed.<br /><br />In the present, Yuki admits to Kakeru that what he wants from Tohru is the unconditional, nurturing love of a mother, not the love of a woman, and yet despite this he is jealous of the growing attraction of Tohru and Kyo.<br /><br />Meanwhile, during rehearsals for Cinderella, their class realizes that their leads are miscast, with Kyo incapable of being Prince Charming or Tohru wicked as a stepsister, nor Saki Hanajima a downtrodden Cinderella. The play is rewritten as semi-Cinderella story and the performance is successful, despite personal, out-of-character outbursts by Tohru, Kyo, and Arisa Uotani. At Tohru's request, Momiji makes a copy of the play's video for Kureno Sohma, so that he can see Uotani's outcry that he come see her.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Yuki sees some girls bullying Machi Kuragi for saying that Yuki is not a prince, which she counters by saying she believes that Yuki is lonely in spite of being surrounded by others. Before anything else can happen, Kakeru comes to save her.<br /><br />This tankōbon is written and illustrated by Natsuki Takaya. For the most part, I really liked the direction of the narrative. The backstory of Yuki Sohma is further deepened and the mystery of Tohru Honda favorite cap has finally been resolved. It is also interesting to see the slow progression of feelings between Kyo Sohma and Tohru Honda, as he quickly ponders and quickly dismissed that she might have feelings for him.<br /><br />All in all, <i>Fruits Basket, Vol. 15</i> is a wonderful continuation to a series that seems intriguing and I cannot wait to read more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8132245793644907217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3258881757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3258881757" />
    <a title="Luisa Maula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82149072-luisa-maula"><img alt="Luisa Maula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589114956p2/82149072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3258881757?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luisa Maula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luisa Maula" href="/user/show/82149072-luisa-maula">Luisa Maula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82149072-luisa-maula?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82149072-luisa-maula?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3258881757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer33068032507032307">This time, it’s Yuki’s turn now to have his own flashback way back in the past. I’ve always considered Yuki a fine gentleman. An attractive person that gets him drawn apart from others, this gives him an impression he’s like a majestic prince to marvel on. <br/><br/>What lays underneath his princely form unbeknownst to everyone, is how awfully introverted he is in person. Yuki’s fans are too busy looking through him in rose tinted glasses that they failed to notice something’s off. They simply thought he’</span>
  <span id="freeText33068032507032307" style="display:none">This time, it’s Yuki’s turn now to have his own flashback way back in the past. I’ve always considered Yuki a fine gentleman. An attractive person that gets him drawn apart from others, this gives him an impression he’s like a majestic prince to marvel on. <br /><br />What lays underneath his princely form unbeknownst to everyone, is how awfully introverted he is in person. Yuki’s fans are too busy looking through him in rose tinted glasses that they failed to notice something’s off. They simply thought he’s just being modest, but it isn’t how it is for the Rat. <br /><br />It’s interesting to fit the puzzle pieces together in figuring out why an individual came out the way they are now. In Yuki’s case, his childhood came out as a tragedy. This resulted to Yuki growing distant and incapable of socializing compared to his other relatives. <br /><br />Not to mention, Akito’s cruel way of discipline did the trick that made Yuki question his self-worth, to the point he’s become so helpless, he doesn’t have anyone to talk to. <br /><br />His own parents are useless and have no right to take such roles, while his older brother’s fortunately making amends for his shortcomings in the past. <br /><br />This is an intriguing volume and it’s piqued my interest since the readers are being enlightened by Yuki’s side for a change. <br /><br />Specifically, this has got to do with the so-called rivalry I thought to come from the Cat and Mouse. This turned out to be much more complicated than that. It’s more difficult whose side I’m on now because of this. <br /><br />On less serious matters aside, I’m living for the mini reunion a couple of Sohma members and Tohru’s friends had here. It’s amusing to see someone getting riled up themselves, a rare occurrence, if you will. Not to mention, I may or may not have come across potential partners suitable for each other here. </span>
  <a data-text-id="33068032507032307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3158613179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3158613179" />
    <a title="Fiona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21373198-fiona"><img alt="Fiona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373663367p2/21373198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

Yuki's developed enough self awareness to realise that his feelings for Tohru aren't actually romantic and he was really looking for the support and love that she gave.   <span id="freeText5854177664007604561" style="display:none">This volume is mostly about the relationships between the characters and how they've developed. Yuki's developed enough self awareness to realise that his feelings for Tohru aren't actually romantic and he was really looking for the support and love that she gave. This is pretty relatable for me as I found myself mistaking what I felt for people as romantic all the time as a teenager when I was first read this, although I never saw that parallel at the time. Yuki's also noticing the burgeoning feelings Kyo and Tohru have for each other, although I don't think Tohru herself has quite worked that out yet.<br /><br />Outside of that there's also the best version of Cinderella I think I've ever seen, mostly because of Hana as Cinderella's desire to shun romance and set up her own restaurant. Tohru's inability to act like a villain is also pretty hilarious, especially as it meant that the Yuki fan club's plan backfired completely. Kyo as a prince and his complete lack of interest in the whole play is brilliant, especially with Uo to back him up.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7304686226801058607">I think I've been holding on well these past 15 volumes, but this one has finally made me cry. Not only that: it managed to make me cry AND laugh on the same volume. Which is why I'm giving it five stars.<br/>Not going to lie, this is a very challenging manga series for me to read.   <span id="freeText7304686226801058607" style="display:none">I think I've been holding on well these past 15 volumes, but this one has finally made me cry. Not only that: it managed to make me cry AND laugh on the same volume. Which is why I'm giving it five stars.<br />Not going to lie, this is a very challenging manga series for me to read. It makes me feel too emotional. Sometimes I have to take a break and just calm down before I keep reading. Because I get too involved with everyone's feelings, their struggle; I feel deeply moved by everything about them. But I think that's a good thing, after all. This story is just so special. The relationships people build with each other... so beautiful. The characters are so well-written; you can't help but love them, and want them to be happy. I love this manga so much.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/91831564-chelsea-best?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2912506386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9218059894486300619">Kyo is truly blossoming in this volume! I LOOVEEE what the characters are becoming. The art style is slowly changing, making each one person look older as if real life time is passing (which is pretty rare in anime/manga). These characters are turning out to be even more beautiful (mentally and physically) than I had remembered during my first read through. I am SO glad I chose to re-read these!!!!! Highly recommend!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18041027576683452099">UGH the feels in this one! I was suspicious of Yuki at first, idk why I just was, but the more I learn about him the more I like his character. Saki Hanajima as Cinderella was seriously funny. Tohru and Kyo are beginning to realize they like each other and I'm like "Yes, take your time, but yes". I'm 100% here for it. </span>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_28628780'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28628780-another-1"><img alt="フルーツバスケットanother 1 (Fruits Basket Another, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1469041623l/28628780._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oFVs4UG2A0Ee6u4+gyya+cuJVPQntSjRrnxt4a+VbmBRc/5z7TYq67VbCi7/6oziwbPs3GisamCUpTzGE5e5Mw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8+HYOSC9bjM71GZ6c2Ir1S+1VPAb/t99BCbF/a84wzYCx0qrjD1HmZBlgmoPpD3OJY/s2FTnncw+/5TaEzoUZQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7981653729064768935"><b>Name (in native language) :</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18983717._' rel='nofollow noopener'>高屋奈月</a><br/><br/>Natsuki Takaya (高屋 奈月 Takaya Natsuki, real name Naka Hatake) is the penname of a Japanese manga artist best-known for creating the series Fruits Basket. She was born on July 7, 1973; (Tanabata). Takaya is left-handed and once revealed that she wanted to be a mangaka since first grade, when her sister started drawing. <br/><br/>She was born in Shizuoka, Japan, but was raised i</span>
  <span id="freeText7981653729064768935" style="display:none"><b>Name (in native language) :</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18983717._" rel="nofollow noopener">高屋奈月</a><br /><br />Natsuki Takaya (高屋 奈月 Takaya Natsuki, real name Naka Hatake) is the penname of a Japanese manga artist best-known for creating the series Fruits Basket. She was born on July 7, 1973; (Tanabata). Takaya is left-handed and once revealed that she wanted to be a mangaka since first grade, when her sister started drawing. <br /><br />She was born in Shizuoka, Japan, but was raised in Tokyo, where she made her debut in 1992. She enjoys video games such as the Final Fantasy series or Sakura Wars, or working on her different manga series, such as Fruits Basket, which is the second best-selling shōjo manga ever in Japan, and the top selling shōjo manga in North America. Fruits Basket has also been adapted into a twenty-six-episode anime series. <br /><br />In 2001, Takaya received a Kodansha Manga Award for shōjo manga for Fruits Basket.<br /><br />According to Takaya (in a sidebar of a Fruits Basket manga volume), she enjoys drawing girls (girly ones) more than she does boys. Takaya also enjoys electronics and music, but dislikes talking about herself. Also revealed in a sidebar of Fruits Basket, Takaya broke her drawing arm (left) after Fruits Basket volume six was published. She had to go into surgery, and as a result, had put Fruits Basket on a brief hiatus. Takaya made a full recovery, but complains that her handwriting had gotten uglier, due to the surgery. During her hospital stay, she gained an interest in baseball.<br /></span>
